--- Page 7 ---
2
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made
the following
                   O R D E R
IA No. 148191/2025 - GRANT OF BAIL
The applicant-appellant has been charged
and convicted for the offence punishable under
Section 302 of the Indian Penal Code, 1860.
 While  the  Trial  Court  acquitted  the
appellant,  the  High  Court  was  pleased  to
reverse  it  and  sentence  him  to  undergo
imprisonment for life.
Taking  note  of  the  conflicting  views
taken by both the Courts, and the period of
incarceration  undergone  by  him,  we  are
inclined  to  suspend  the  sentence  of  the
appellant, during the pendency of his appeal.
Accordingly,  the  sentence  of  the
appellant is suspended and he is granted bail,
during the pendency of the appeal, on terms
and conditions to the satisfaction of the
Trial Court.

--- Page 8 ---
3
List the appeal in the second week of
February, 2027.
(ASHA SUNDRIYAL)                  (POONAM VAID)

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.4441/2019
NACHHATTAR SINGH (D) THROUGH LRS     Appellant(s)
VERSUS
JAGTAR SINGH & ANR.        Respondent(s)
O R D E R
1. Today,  learned  counsel  for  the  respondent
no.1 has handed over a copy of the compromise deed
dated 25.07.2022 executed between petitioner and
respondent No.1 as well as its translated copy.
The said translated copy reads as under:
COMPROMISE DEED
We,  Nachhattar  Kaur,  widow  and  Gursewak  Singh,
Gurmeet Singh, Sukhwinder Kaur, Harpreet Kaur and
Baljeet Kaur,  children of Nacchhattar Singh (Party No.1)
and Jagtar Singh, son of Gurdeep Singh son of Bakhtawar
Singh  (Party  No.2),  residents  of  Village  Bandi,  Tehsil
Bathinda, hereby execute this compromise Deed as under:
1.That  a  dispute  had  arisen  between  both  the  parties
regarding  land  comprised  in  Khasra  No.746/1  (Sale
Deed/Wasika  No.669  dated  12.03.1992),  and  on
account thereof litigation remained pending before different
Courts. At present, the said dispute is pending before the
Hon’ble Supreme Court of India vide S.L.P. (Civil) No.8687
1

--- Page 12 ---
of 2017, wherein a stay order has been granted. Now, the
respectable persons of the village have brought about an
amicable settlement between both the parties. As per the
said compromise, the disputed land has been divided equally
between both the parties. Party No.2 shall execute and get
registered the Sale Deed in favour of Party No.1 in respect of
one-half share of the disputed land. Thereafter, after proper
measurement,  the  land  shall  be  divided  equally  between
both the parties at the spot. Both the parties shall be bound
to  submit  this  written  compromise  before  the  Hon’ble
Supreme Court in accordance with the procedure prescribed
by law. Thereafter, neither party shall have any objection or
claim against the other. The trees standing on the land shall
also be divided equally. The Government watercourse (Khal)
shall subsequently be laid through the middle of the said 16
Marlas, and thereafter the land of both the parties shall be
carved out equally. The responsibility for withdrawal of the
case and for getting the stay order vacated shall be that of
Party  No.1.  If  either  party  resiles  from  this  written
compromise, the defaulting party shall be liable to pay a
sum of  ₹10,00,000/-  (Rupees Ten Lakhs only)  to  the
other  party as compensation.  Therefore,  being in our  full
senses and of our own free will, without any pressure or
coercion, we have executed this Compromise Deed in the
presence of the witnesses on  25.07.2022,  so that it may
serve as evidence whenever required.
Party No.1
 Nachhattar Kaur
 Gursewak Singh
 Gurmeet Singh
 Sukhwinder Kaur
 Harpreet Kaur
 Baljeet Kaur
Party No.2
2

--- Page 13 ---
 Jagtar Singh
Witnesses
1. Gurjit Singh, Numberdar, Village Bandi.
2. Manjit Singh, son of Raghvir Singh, resident of Village
Bandi.
3. Jagtar Singh, son of Gurdev Singh, resident of Village
Bandi.
4. Darshan  Singh,  son  of  Mukand  Singh,  resident  of
Village Bandi.
5. Resham  Singh,  son  of  Gurdeep  Singh,  resident  of
Village Bandi.
6. Jagjit Singh, son of Joginder Singh, resident of Village
Bandi.
2. Learned counsel for petitioner states that
respondent no.1 is not complying with the terms
and conditions mentioned in the compromise deed.
3. Learned  counsel  for  the  respondent  no.1
assures and undertakes to this Court that the
terms and conditions of the said compromise deed
shall be complied with in letter and spirit.
4. The said statement is taken on record and the
respondent no.1 is held bound by the statement.
5. Accordingly,  the  present  Civil  Appeal  is
disposed of in terms of the said compromise deed
along with all pending applications.

--- Page 16 ---
1
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.                  OF 2026  
(Arising out of SLP (C) No. 14117 of 2023)
MOHAMMAD YUNUS & ORS.    … APPELLANTS
VERSUS
SHAKUR KHAN & ORS.   … RESPONDENTS
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. Being dissatisfied with the amount of compensation
awarded  and  assailing  the  finding  of  contributory
negligence recorded vide order dated 16.09.2021 by the
High  Court  of  Madhya  Pradesh,  Bench  at  Indore,  the
present appeal has been filed by the claimants seeking
enhancement.
3. In the facts of the case, it is not in dispute that
the deceased was met with an accident on 07.03.2010 while
driving Maruti Zen Car and died in the road accident.
4. In our view, the short question that falls for our
consideration  is  whether  the  monthly  income  of  the

--- Page 17 ---
2
deceased as accepted at Rs. 4,000/- per month by the High
Court on the date of accident is just or on the lower
side. 
5. After hearing  and considering  the fact  that the
deceased was performing work of remolding and trading of
old tyres, in our view, the income of Rs. 4,000/- per
month as accepted was on lower side. The accident took
place on 07.03.2010, however, we may accept earning of
Rs.  6,000/-  per  month.  Looking  to  the  number  of
dependents, if we deduct 1/4 th towards personal expenses,
as such per month dependency comes to Rs. 4,500/-, i.e.,
Rs. 54,000/- per annum. By adding future prospects at the
rate of 40%, the amount comes to Rs. 75,600/- per annum.
Since the deceased was 38 years of age, however, the
multiplier of 15 is applicable, thereby the amount of
loss of dependency comes to Rs. 11,34,000/-. 
6. We further add Rs. 1,50,000/- in the conventional
heads. As such the total amount of compensation comes to
Rs. 12,84,000/-. Since, the deceased was driving the car
and met with an accident by collision with stationary

--- Page 18 ---
3
truck, therefore, the finding of contributory negligence
to the extent of 50% and the direction to pay and
recover,  recorded  by  the  High  Court  deserves  to  be
maintained. 
7. In view of the foregoing the appeal stands allowed in
part. The finding of contributory negligence, pay and
recover of the High court is hereby maintained, though,
the amount of compensation is enhanced to Rs.12,84,000/-.
In view of the contributory negligence the sum payable
comes to Rs. 6,42,000/-. The said amount along with
interest @ 7 per cent be paid within a period of eight
weeks adjusting the amount already paid if any. Pending
applications, if any, shall also stand disposed of.
……………………………………………………………,J.
           [J.K. MAHESHWARI]
……………………………………………………………,J.
 [ATUL S. CHANDURKAR]
New Delhi;
March 18, 2026.

                   Mr. Aashwyn Singh, Adv.
                   Ms. Ananya Dutta, Adv.
                   Mr. Aniket Kanhaua, Adv.
                   Mr. Nitin Saluja, AOR
Mr. Amit Kapur, Adv.*
Mr. B. Ranganthan, Adv.*                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Heard Mr. Tushar Mehta, learned Solicitor General for the
appellant, Dr. Abhishek Manu Singhvi, learned Senior Counsel,

--- Page 21 ---
2
Mr. Amit Kapur, Mr. B. Ranganthan and Mr. Shri Venkatesh,
learned  Senior  Counsel/learned  Counsel  appearing  for  the
respondent(s) on caveat.
2. The present Civil Appeals concern directly with the issue
whether  the  action  of  the  Delhi  Electricity  Regulatory
Commission (for short, ‘DERC’) to initiate the process of
audit  of  the  distribution  companies  of  Delhi  by  the
Comptroller and Auditor General of India (for short, ‘CAG’) is
legally permissible. The Appellate Tribunal for Electricity
(for short, ‘APTEL’) on this issue has held that the action of
the DERC in entrusting the strict and intensive audit as
directed by this Court of the Delhi discoms to CAG is in
contravention of the statutory provisions. After holding so,
the  APTEL  has  directed  DERC  ‘to  appoint  any  Chartered
Accountant  within  one  week  from  today’  with  specific
directions to conclude the strict and intensive audit of the
Delhi Discoms (paragraph 40 of the impugned order).
3. We have heard learned Senior Counsel and learned Counsel
on this issue.
4. Issue notice.
5. Till further orders, there shall be a stay of operation
of the direction to DERC given at paragraph 40 of the APTEL’s
order  (impugned  order)  with  regard  to  the  direction  of
appointment of any Chartered Accountant for the purpose of
audit. At the same time, till the Civil Appeals are decided,
the CAG also shall not proceed with the audit.
6. During the course of the arguments, Mr. Tushar Mehta,

--- Page 22 ---
3
learned Solicitor General for India has raised an issue that
the audit needs to be completed before recoveries can be
effected  from  the  consumers.  He  places  reliance  on  the
judgment  of  this  Court  in  W.P.(C)No.104/2014  especially
paragraph 71, clause (vi) thereto, which reads as follows:
“Regulatory Commissions must provide the trajectory
and roadmap for liquidation of the existing regulatory
asset, which will include a provision for dealing with
carrying  costs.  Regulatory  Commissions  must  also
undertake  strict  and  intensive  audit  of  the
circumstances in which the distribution companies have
continued without recovery of the regulatory asset.”
7. On the other hand learned Senior Counsel/learned Counsel
appearing for the distribution companies submit that the issue
of audit and the issue of recovery pursuant to the creating
of the regulatory assets are independent. Learned counsels
submits that the Civil Appeals are confined to the issue of
audit and the aspect of liquidation which has been dealt with
separately in the impugned order, has not been called in
question.
8. Mr. Tushar Mehta, learned Solicitor General for India, in
response submits that, that is only a matter of technicality
as they propose to file a Civil Appeal on that aspect also.
9. Learned Solicitor General for India also draws attention
to the grounds to show that unless the audit is completed,
permitting recovery from the consumers will be putting the
cart before the horse.
10. Since this aspect of the matter involves interpretation

--- Page 23 ---
4
of  the  judgment  of  this  Court  dated  06.08.2025  in  W.P.
(C)No.104/2014, we are of the opinion that this matter should
be heard by the Hon’ble Judges who were part of that Bench,
subject to, of course, orders from Hon’ble the Chief Justice
of India.
11. List these matters on 15th July, 2026.
12. Let the papers of these matters be placed before Hon’ble
the Chief Justice of India.
13. Till 15th July, 2026, there shall be a status quo on all
aspects.
14. List the impleadment application along with the main
matters.
(NIRMALA NEGI)                                  (MANOJ KUMAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                        COURT MASTER (NSH)
*appearance not given

O R D E R
Heard learned counsel appearing for the appellant
and perused the material available on record.
2. Delay in re-filing is condoned.
3. Delay in filing is condoned.
4. The present Civil Appeal arises out of the judgment
and order dated 27th February, 2026, passed by the National
Company Law Appellate Tribunal, Principal Bench, New Delhi,
in Company Appeal (AT)(Insolvency) No.357 of 2026. 
5. By the impugned judgment and order, the Appellate
Tribunal dismissed the appeal preferred by the appellant,
observing as under:
“Appellant is an operational creditor and under the
scheme of the IBC and the CIRP Regulation, he is
not entitled for the copy of the Resolution Plan.
When the court has granted liberty to the Appellant
to challenge the plan, it is always open for the
Appellant to file appropriate Application objecting
to the new Resolution Plan raising all permissible
pleas in accordance with law.” 
6.  Having considered the matter in its entirety and
perusing the material available on record, we do not find
1

--- Page 33 ---
any good ground to interfere with the impugned judgment and
order.
7. Accordingly, the Civil Appeal stands dismissed.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.

Chaudhri, learned Senior Counsel for the petitioner to clarify

Senior Counsel for the petitioner submits that the petitioner
was pursuing the present matter(s) on the apprehension that
the orders in the present matter(s) will come in the way of

3. We are of the opinion that the appropriate remedy will be
to pursue the anticipatory bail application.
4. Learned Senior Counsel for the petitioner further submits
that they have taken steps for moving the anticipatory bail
application before the High Court.
5. We direct that in case the anticipatory bail application
is filed, it will be decided in accordance with law and on its
own merits uninfluenced by the impugned order. However, the
Investigating Agency will be at liberty to point out the
impugned order if they seek to rely on the conduct of the
petitioner and equally the petitioner will also be at liberty
to show that there was no adverse conduct on the part of the
petitioner.
6. With these observations, the Special Leave Petitions are
disposed of.

               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition for Special Leave to Appeal (Crl.) No.10629/2024
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 22-01-2024 
in CRMM No. 39200/2022 passed by the High Court of Punjab & Haryana
at Chandigarh]
SURINDER SINGH                                        Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
KULVIR KAUR & ANR.                                    Respondent(s)
IA No. 165889/2024 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
 
Date : 03-07-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE MANMOHAN 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE K. VINOD CHANDRAN
For Petitioner(s) : Mr. Lalltaksh Joshi, AOR
                   
For Respondent(s) : Mr. Vaibhav Sehgal, Adv.
                   Ms. Shivya Sehgal, Adv.
                   Mr. Hitesh Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Umesh, Adv.
                   Mr. Shravya Doomra, Adv.
                   Mr. R. C. Kaushik, AOR
                   
                   Mr. Siddhant Sharma, AOR
                   Mr. Akshay Malhotra, Adv.
                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The present special leave petition has been filed
challenging the judgment and order dated 22.01.2024 passed
by the Punjab and Haryana High Court at Chandigarh in CRM-
M-39200 of 2022 (O&M) whereby the High Court set aside the
order dated 26.07.2022 passed by the Judicial Magistrate,
1st Class, Phagwara in CRM/29/2020 declining the protest
1

--- Page 39 ---
petition filed by the Respondent No.1 against the final
report dated 12.09.2019 presented by the investigating
agency whereby the Petitioner, his wife and daughter were
declared innocent.
2. Learned counsel for the petitioner submits that the
impugned order had been passed behind the back of the
petitioner without arraying him as a party or issuing him
notice.
3. Learned  counsel  for  respondent  No.1  states  that
keeping in view the nature of prayer made in the High
Court, the issuance of notice to the petitioner in the
present petition was not called for.
4. This Court is of the view that if a complainant
challenges the order passed by the Magistrate terminating
the proceedings against persons alleged to have committed
an offence, then by virtue of Section 401(2) CrPC, the
suspects get the right of hearing before the High Court,
although, such order was passed by the Magistrate without
their participation.[See: Manharibhai Muljibhai Kakadia &
Anr. vs. Shaileshbhai Mohanbhai Patel & Ors., (2012) 10 SCC
517 and  Subhash  Sahebrao  Deshmukh  vs.  Satish  Atmaram
Talekar & Ors., (2020) 6 SCC 625].
5. Consequently, the impugned order is set aside and the
matter is remanded back to the High Court for fresh hearing
and  determination.  The  petitioner  shall  be  given  an
opportunity of hearing before the High Court.
2

--- Page 40 ---
6. Needless to state, the High Court shall decide the
matter  on  its  own  without  being  influenced  by  any
observation made by this Court.  The rights and contentions
of all the parties are left open.
7. The Special Leave Petition stands disposed of along
with all pending applications.
(KRITIKA TIWARI)                                (DIVYA BABBAR)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

Date : 03-07-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE MANMOHAN 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE K. VINOD CHANDRAN
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Anil Kaushik, A.S.G.
                   Mr. Ajay Kumar Singh, AOR
                   Mr. Yatharth Singh, Adv.
                   Mr. Divyansh Singh, Adv.  
Mr. Sanjay Sharawat, Sr. Adv.
                   Mr. Ravi Kant, Adv.
                   Mr. Mayank Manish, Adv.
                   Mr. Vineet Upadhyay, Adv.
                   Mr. Chandra Prakash, AOR
                   Mr. Jayant Dubey, Adv.
                   Mr. Vivek Singh, Adv.
                   Mr. C. P. Rajwar, Adv.
1

--- Page 42 ---
                   Mr. Rohan Chandra, Adv.                 
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The Applicants, Pharmacy Council of India and All India
Council for Technical Education, seek extension of time
schedule for approval process of institutions, grant of
admission and completion of admission process laid down
by this Court fourteen (14) years ago in Parshavanath
Charitable Trust Vs. All India Council for Technical
Education, (2013) 3 SCC 385.
2. It seems that such applications have been filed in the
routine for the past few years.
3. This Court is of the considered view that extension of
even one deadline has a cascading effect, inasmuch as,
the last date for grant of refusal of approval by the
University/State  Government,  conduct  of  entrance
examination, counselling and last date for admission
get extended. 
4. Further, the extension of even one deadline not only
affects the academic calendar but also puts a lot of
pressure on other institutions like the High Courts. 
5. Needless to state that the Regulators like Pharmacy
2

--- Page 43 ---
Council of India and All India Council for Technical
Education ‘ need to shape up ’ and comply with the
binding directions issued by this Court and not seek
extensions in routine. 
6. At this stage, learned Additional Solicitor General
prays for and is permitted to file an affidavit on or
before 07.07.2026. 
7. List the matters on 08.07.2026.
(KRITIKA TIWARI)                                (DIVYA BABBAR)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
We have heard the learned Solicitor General
appearing for the petitioner-State and the learned
counsel appearing for the respondent.
Learned Solicitor General submits that both the
Courts have not considered the relevant materials
against the respondent, including the recording made
by the learned Judicial Magistrate on the earlier

--- Page 65 ---
2
occasion.  Apart  from  the  nature  of  allegations
against the respondent which are quite serious, the
fact that three earlier bail applications have been
rejected by the Trial Court and the present plea has
not been raised earlier, have not been considered by
both the Courts. A further submission has been made
that it is not a case of grounds of arrest not being
served,  but  is  one  of  not  containing  adequate
reasons, apart from a typographical error.
Reliance has been placed on the order passed by
the learned Judicial Magistrate in the presence of
the respondent.
Learned counsel appearing for the respondent on
caveat seeks some time to file the counter affidavit
and is permitted to do so.  It is also submitted by
him that the order granting bail has already been
given  effect  to  and  the  respondent  has  been
released.
Taking note of the above submissions, we are
inclined to list the matter for further hearing next
Thursday, i.e. on 9th July, 2026.
In the meantime, the learned counsel appearing
for the petitioner is permitted to file additional
documents.

for the petitioner.

the Letter of Intent (for short, ‘LOI’) was dated 21.03.2023
and the one year for compliance of the conditionalities would
expire on 20.03.2024. Learned Senior Counsel for the petitioner

--- Page 93 ---
2
also draws attention to the clause which provides that this
period is extendable at the behest of the State.
3. Learned Senior Counsel for the petitioner submits that
the  name  change  of  the  petitioner-entity  happened  on
01.06.2023. The Scheme of Prospecting which the petitioner was
obliged to furnish was done on 23.08.2023. On 27.10.2023, the
name change was noted by the Authority concerned. On 08.03.2024
before the expiry of the one year period, application for
extension was made and since no reply was forthcoming, the writ
petition was filed on 30.01.2025. Thereafter, learned Senior
Counsel  for  the  petitioner  fairly  points  out  that  a
cancellation order has been made on 22.04.2025. Learned Senior
Counsel for the petitioner submits that the petitioner has done
everything  under  its  control  and  under  the  facts  and
circumstances, there was a power coupled with the duty on the
part of the respondent-State to consider and pass the orders of
extension.
4. Issue notice, returnable on 07th September, 2026.
5. Till further orders,  status quo  as on today, shall be
maintained and there shall be an injunction restraining the
encashment of the bank guarantee.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. It seems to us that various statutes such as the Pharmacy Act,
1948 whereunder some statutory bodies, perceived to be autonomous,
are constituted to run affairs of professional/scientific/technical
education,  need  to  be  revisited  in  light  of  the  changing
circumstances.  
2. We, therefore, request the learned Attorney General for India
to assist us on the broader issue.  Meanwhile, the Registry shall
prepare a list of such like statutes.
3. Meanwhile, the prayer for interim stay is declined.
4. List on 03.08.2026.

Section 216 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1973.
